             <div class="sqs-block summary-v2-block sqs-block-summary-v2" data-block-json='{"hSize":null,"floatDir":null,"collectionId":"50c9c511e4b0a97682fac90c","design":"carousel","headerText":"","textSize":"medium","pageSize":30,"imageAspectRatio":"1","columnWidth":270,"gutter":60,"listImageSize":30,"listImageAlignment":"left","slidesPerRow":4,"textAlignment":"center","showTitle":true,"showThumbnail":true,"showExcerpt":true,"showReadMoreLink":true,"showPrice":true,"productQuickViewEnabled":false,"showPastOrUpcomingEvents":"Upcoming","metadataPosition":"below-content","primaryMetadata":"none","secondaryMetadata":"none","filter":{},"autoCrop":true,"lightbox":false,"mixedContent":true,"blockId":"2ad05e2d837599b24adb"}' data-block-type="55" id="block-yui_3_10_1_1_1398939395651_27509">
              <div class="sqs-block-content">
               <div class=" summary-block-wrapper summary-block-collection-type-blog summary-block-setting-text-size-medium summary-block-setting-text-align-center summary-block-setting-design-carousel summary-block-setting-design-list-thumbnail-left summary-block-setting-metadata-position-below-content summary-block-setting-primary-metadata-none summary-block-setting-secondary-metadata-none summary-block-setting-show-thumbnail summary-block-setting-show-title summary-block-setting-show-price summary-block-setting-show-excerpt summary-block-setting-show-read-more-link sqs-gallery-design-carousel ">
                <div class="summary-item-list-container sqs-gallery-container">
                 <header class="summary-block-header">
                  <!-- Collection Title -->
                  <div class="summary-heading">
                   <span class="summary-collection-title">
                    General BA Matters
                   </span>
                  </div>
                  <!-- Carousel Nav -->
                  <div class="summary-carousel-pager sqs-gallery-controls">
                   <span class="summary-carousel-pager-next next">
                   </span>
                   <span class="summary-carousel-pager-prev previous">
                   </span>

                 <div class="summary-item-list sqs-gallery">
                  <div class=" summary-item summary-item-record-type-text sqs-gallery-design-carousel-slide summary-item-has-thumbnail summary-item-has-excerpt summary-item-has-cats summary-item-has-tags summary-item-has-author summary-item-has-comments-enabled ">
                   <!-- Thumbnail -->
                   <div class="summary-thumbnail-outer-container">
                    <a class="summary-thumbnail-container sqs-gallery-image-container" data-description="" data-title="5 Simple Ways BAs Can Avoid Repeating Mistakes From Past Projects" href="/blog/2018/5/6/5-simple-ways-bas-can-avoid-repeating-mistakes-from-past-projects">
                     <div class="summary-thumbnail img-wrapper">
                      <!-- Main Image -->
                      <img alt="5 Simple Ways BAs Can Avoid Repeating Mistakes From Past Projects" class="summary-thumbnail-image" data-image="https://static1.squarespace.com/static/50c9c50fe4b0a97682fac903/50c9c511e4b0a97682fac90c/5aef51bb352f535b34d9b136/1525634532081/oops.jpg" data-image-dimensions="1000x991" data-image-focal-point="0.5,0.5" data-load="false" data-src="https://static1.squarespace.com/static/50c9c50fe4b0a97682fac903/50c9c511e4b0a97682fac90c/5aef51bb352f535b34d9b136/1525634532081/oops.jpg"/>
                     </div>
                    </a>
                    <!-- Products: Quick View -->
                   </div>
                   <div class="summary-content sqs-gallery-meta-container">
                    <!-- Metadata (Above Title) -->
                    <div class="summary-metadata-container summary-metadata-container--above-title">
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--primary">
                     </div>
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--secondary">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Title -->
                    <div class="summary-title">
                     <a class="summary-title-link" href="/blog/2018/5/6/5-simple-ways-bas-can-avoid-repeating-mistakes-from-past-projects">
                      5 Simple Ways BAs Can Avoid Repeating Mistakes From Past Projects
                     </a>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Metadata (Below Title) -->
                    <div class="summary-metadata-container summary-metadata-container--below-title">
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--primary">
                     </div>
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--secondary">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Excerpt -->
                    <div class="summary-excerpt">
                     <p style="white-space: pre-wrap;">
                      Once you embark on a new business analyst job or project, chances are that you will try to avoid past mistakes and look for ways in which you can deliver better results.
                     </p>
                     <p style="white-space: pre-wrap;">
                      A lot can be said for this motivation. The beginning of a project is usually an opportunity for a fresh start. Regardless of how advanced your business analysis skills are, or how fine-tuned your business analysis process is, there is always room to do better.
                      <strong>
                       Guest post by Jason Hartman.
                      </strong>
                     </p>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Read More Link -->
                    <a class="summary-read-more-link" href="/blog/2018/5/6/5-simple-ways-bas-can-avoid-repeating-mistakes-from-past-projects">
                     Read More 
                    </a>
                    <!-- Metadata (Below Content) -->
                    <div class="summary-metadata-container summary-metadata-container--below-content">
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--primary">
                     </div>
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--secondary">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                   </div>
                   <!-- End .summary-content -->
                  </div>
                  <!-- End .summary-item -->
                  <div class=" summary-item summary-item-record-type-text sqs-gallery-design-carousel-slide summary-item-has-excerpt summary-item-has-cats summary-item-has-tags summary-item-has-author summary-item-has-comments-enabled ">
                   <!-- Thumbnail -->
                   <div class="summary-content sqs-gallery-meta-container">
                    <!-- Metadata (Above Title) -->
                    <div class="summary-metadata-container summary-metadata-container--above-title">
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--primary">
                     </div>
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--secondary">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Title -->
                    <div class="summary-title">
                     <a class="summary-title-link" href="/blog/2018/4/23/how-to-get-stakeholders-to-open-up-during-elicitation-sessions">
                      How to Get Stakeholders to Open Up During Elicitation Sessions
                     </a>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Metadata (Below Title) -->
                    <div class="summary-metadata-container summary-metadata-container--below-title">
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--primary">
                     </div>
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--secondary">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Excerpt -->
                    <div class="summary-excerpt">
                     <p>
                      If youve worked as a Business Analyst for a while, youve probably encountered stakeholders who appear quite economical with information. You know theres more to the issue than theyre letting on. The key question is, how can you get stakeholders to open up when conducting elicitation events like interviews or workshop sessions?
                     </p>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Read More Link -->
                    <a class="summary-read-more-link" href="/blog/2018/4/23/how-to-get-stakeholders-to-open-up-during-elicitation-sessions">
                     Read More 
                    </a>
                    <!-- Metadata (Below Content) -->
                    <div class="summary-metadata-container summary-metadata-container--below-content">
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--primary">
                     </div>
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--secondary">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                   </div>

                  </div>

                   <!-- Thumbnail -->
                   <div class="summary-thumbnail-outer-container">
                    <a class="summary-thumbnail-container sqs-gallery-image-container" data-description="" data-title="What Business Analysts Can Learn From Technical Writers" href="/blog/2018/4/17/what-business-analysts-can-learn-from-technical-writers">
                     <div class="summary-thumbnail img-wrapper">
                      <!-- Main Image -->

                    <!-- Title -->
                    <div class="summary-title">
                     <a class="summary-title-link" href="/blog/2018/4/17/what-business-analysts-can-learn-from-technical-writers">
                      What Business Analysts Can Learn From Technical Writers
                     </a>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Metadata (Below Title) -->
                    <div class="summary-metadata-container summary-metadata-container--below-title">
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--primary">
                     </div>
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--secondary">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Excerpt -->
                    <div class="summary-excerpt">
                     <p>
                      Most of my time, especially at the tail end of software development projects, is spent preparing user guides for end users. I try to be creative by including screenshots and business process models so that readers can completely understand what the automated processes are about, and how the supporting business applications work.As a BA, you may find yourself in a situation where you need to prepare user guides for end users.
                     </p>

                     </a>

                    <!-- Metadata (Below Title) -->
                    <div class="summary-metadata-container summary-metadata-container--below-title">

                    <!-- Excerpt -->
                    <div class="summary-excerpt">
                     <p>
                      Transferrable skills are a core set of skills and abilities, which can be applied to other jobs and industries. Though most examples you will see are related to soft skills like communication, listening, leadership, etc, transferrable skills extend beyond these and its extremely important to identify them when thinking of a career change or advancement.
                     </p>

                    <div class="summary-title">
                     <a class="summary-title-link" href="/blog/2018/1/3/confirmation-bias-what-bas-can-learn-from-data-scientists">
                      Confirmation Bias: What BAs Can Learn From Data Scientists
                     </a>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Metadata (Below Title) -->
                    <div class="summary-metadata-container summary-metadata-container--below-title">
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--primary">
                     </div>
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--secondary">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Excerpt -->
                    <div class="summary-excerpt">
                     <p>
                      When we have a strong belief about something or a bias towards a particular opinion, we consciously or unconsciously seek out evidence that validates what we already believe.When we come across contrary evidence, our default behaviour is to ignore it, diminish it or in some cases, conclude that its wrong prematurely without exploring its merits.
                     </p>

                    <!-- Title -->
                    <div class="summary-title">
                     <a class="summary-title-link" href="/blog/2017/12/16/business-analysts-the-anchor-effect">
                      Business Analysts &amp; The Anchor Effect
                     </a>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Metadata (Below Title) -->
                    <div class="summary-metadata-container summary-metadata-container--below-title">
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--primary">
                     </div>

                     </div>

                    <!-- Excerpt -->
                    <div class="summary-excerpt">
                     <p>
                      Imagine a component in your car requires a fix. You approach your mechanic and he gives you a quote. This quote (assuming youve never had to pay for this part before and you have no prior knowledge of how much it costs) becomes the reference point from which you begin negotiation. This reference point is called an anchor and its effects can be seen in everyday situations.
                     </p>

                    <div class="summary-excerpt">
                     <p>
                      When elicitation focuses on identifying exceptions and failure points, its a form of risk management. The idea is to find potential solutions to these questions and include them as part of requirements to reduce the probability of missing out on critical requirements.

                     </a>

                    <!-- Excerpt -->
                    <div class="summary-excerpt">
                     <p>
                      Governance seems to be one of those frightening words that threaten to stop an Agile transformation effort dead in its tracks. Ive been hearing it whispered, and even screamed once or twice, quite a lot recently. Theres no big surprise here. As big corporations and Government agencies get increasingly fascinated by frameworks like Scrum, they are mandating their IT departments to go agile and then, sooner or latergovernance!

                      <img alt="The Business Analyst &amp; Project Manager Collaboration: Identifying The Various Costs Involved In A Business Case" class="summary-thumbnail-image" data-image="https://static1.squarespace.com/static/50c9c50fe4b0a97682fac903/50c9c511e4b0a97682fac90c/590dc64917bffcc3aa0e72c1/1514625232523/Depositphotos_138527976_m-2015.jpg" data-image-dimensions="1000x756" data-image-focal-point="0.5,0.5" data-load="false" data-src="https://static1.squarespace.com/static/50c9c50fe4b0a97682fac903/50c9c511e4b0a97682fac90c/590dc64917bffcc3aa0e72c1/1514625232523/Depositphotos_138527976_m-2015.jpg"/>

                    <!-- Title -->
                    <div class="summary-title">
                     <a class="summary-title-link" href="/blog/2017/5/6/the-business-analystproject-manager-collaboration-identifying-the-various-costs-involved-in-writing-a-business-case">
                      The Business Analyst &amp; Project Manager Collaboration: Identifying The Various Costs Involved In A Business Case
                     </a>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Metadata (Below Title) -->
                    <div class="summary-metadata-container summary-metadata-container--below-title">
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--primary">
                     </div>
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--secondary">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Excerpt -->
                    <div class="summary-excerpt">
                     <p>
                      In preparing a business case, the business analyst is often required to conduct some measure of cost analysis. When highlighting the benefits associated with an initiative, it is extremely important to also indicate the costs that will go along with implementing the initiative. Information regarding costs is particularly important in making go or no-go decisions when deciding which projects to implement. The business analyst should work with the project manager to identify these costs and arrive at realistic estimates.
                     </p>
                    </div>

                    <a class="summary-thumbnail-container sqs-gallery-image-container" data-description="" data-title="How Should BAs Relate With Other Project Stakeholders?" href="/blog/2017/4/11/how-should-bas-relate-with-other-project-stakeholders">
                     <div class="summary-thumbnail img-wrapper">
                      <!-- Main Image -->
                      <img alt="How Should BAs Relate With Other Project Stakeholders?" class="summary-thumbnail-image" data-image="https://static1.squarespace.com/static/50c9c50fe4b0a97682fac903/50c9c511e4b0a97682fac90c/58ec857a2e69cffbfbeb0184/1514619298488/ID-100275905.jpg" data-image-dimensions="400x266" data-image-focal-point="0.5,0.5" data-load="false" data-src="https://static1.squarespace.com/static/50c9c50fe4b0a97682fac903/50c9c511e4b0a97682fac90c/58ec857a2e69cffbfbeb0184/1514619298488/ID-100275905.jpg"/>
                     </div>
                    </a>
                    <!-- Products: Quick View -->
                   </div>
                   <div class="summary-content sqs-gallery-meta-container">
                    <!-- Metadata (Above Title) -->
                    <div class="summary-metadata-container summary-metadata-container--above-title">
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--primary">
                     </div>
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--secondary">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Title -->
                    <div class="summary-title">
                     <a class="summary-title-link" href="/blog/2017/4/11/how-should-bas-relate-with-other-project-stakeholders">
                      How Should BAs Relate With Other Project Stakeholders?
                     </a>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Metadata (Below Title) -->
                    <div class="summary-metadata-container summary-metadata-container--below-title">
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--primary">
                     </div>
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--secondary">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Excerpt -->
                    <div class="summary-excerpt">
                     <p>
                      According to Stephen Ward &amp; Chris Chapman in their piece,
                      <a href="http://www.tandfonline.com/doi/abs/10.1080/01446190801998708">
                       Stakeholders and uncertainty management in projects
                      </a>
                      , Stakeholders are a major source of uncertainty on projects and this uncertainty stems from whom these stakeholders are, their motives, and how they can influence a project.
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      It is this uncertainty that constitutes risks to the project. BAs should relate with other project stakeholders to overcome this uncertainty by improving their ability to convince stakeholders to see things their way, thereby influencing the course of the project.
                     </p>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Read More Link -->
                    <a class="summary-read-more-link" href="/blog/2017/4/11/how-should-bas-relate-with-other-project-stakeholders">

                     <div class="summary-thumbnail img-wrapper">
                      <!-- Main Image -->
                      <img alt="5 Things Business Analysts Should Learn From UX Designers" class="summary-thumbnail-image" data-image="https://static1.squarespace.com/static/50c9c50fe4b0a97682fac903/50c9c511e4b0a97682fac90c/58e9b01edb29d654dc1a8377/1491841406916/ux-512x270-2.png" data-image-dimensions="512x270" data-image-focal-point="0.5,0.5" data-load="false" data-src="https://static1.squarespace.com/static/50c9c50fe4b0a97682fac903/50c9c511e4b0a97682fac90c/58e9b01edb29d654dc1a8377/1491841406916/ux-512x270-2.png"/>
                     </div>

                    <!-- Metadata (Above Title) -->

                    <!-- Title -->
                    <div class="summary-title">
                     <a class="summary-title-link" href="/blog/2017/4/9/5-things-business-analysts-should-learn-from-ux-designers">
                      5 Things Business Analysts Should Learn From UX Designers
                     </a>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Metadata (Below Title) -->
                    <div class="summary-metadata-container summary-metadata-container--below-title">
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--primary">
                     </div>
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--secondary">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Excerpt -->
                    <div class="summary-excerpt">
                     <p>
                      BAs can learn a lot from UXers, that much is certain. But perhaps the most valuable thing the two disciplines can learn from each other is working together. Both roles have the same ultimate aimto produce a product that has business value and meets users needs. The approaches may differ but are far from conflicting: BAs create value by delivering good features and functions, UXers by delivering good experiences.
                      <strong>
                       Guest Post by
                       <em>
                        Cassandra Naji
                       </em>
                      </strong>
                     </p>

                    <div class="summary-title">
                     <a class="summary-title-link" href="/blog/2017/2/18/why-do-requirements-need-to-be-detailed-what-level-of-detail-is-enough">
                      Why Do Requirements Need To Be Detailed &amp; What Level Of Detail Is Enough?
                     </a>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Metadata (Below Title) -->
                    <div class="summary-metadata-container summary-metadata-container--below-title">
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--primary">

                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--secondary">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Excerpt -->
                    <div class="summary-excerpt">
                     <p>
                      As development practices change, so do the reasons why we write requirements and the level of detail we go into with Requirements Specification Documents. Even seasoned business analysts have at one point or the other asked themselves, What level of detail is enough?. The answer to this seemingly simple question is inseparably intertwined with the reason why we write requirements in the first place: so that they can be read, understood, and implemented.
                     </p>

                    <!-- Title -->
                    <div class="summary-title">
                     <a class="summary-title-link" href="/business-analyst-career/2016/11/26/conflict-management-in-business-teams">
                      Conflict Management In Business Teams
                     </a>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Metadata (Below Title) -->
                    <div class="summary-metadata-container summary-metadata-container--below-title">
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--primary">
                     </div>
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--secondary">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Excerpt -->
                    <div class="summary-excerpt">
                     <p>
                      Conflicts are bound to arise when people with different views and different backgrounds work together. There is hardly any profession where people do not work in teams or groups where conflicts are inevitable. No matter how hard one tries to get used to the differences in their teams, the probability of conflicts is always there. Be it a corporate or a sports unit/team, all have, at one time or the other, had to face conflict.
                     </p>

                    <!-- Excerpt -->
                    <div class="summary-excerpt">
                     <p>
                      The idea of a business analyst wearing multiple hats is certainly important in ensuring that requirement definitions identified at the beginning of a project do not get lost along the way. One of the key strengths a business analyst possesses which needs to trickle down to other sections of the business is their understanding of business requirements.

                    <div class="summary-excerpt">
                     <p style="white-space: pre-wrap;">
                      As a practising BA Consultant for the past25 years, I have come across many business analysis tools.                       <img alt="So, What's An API?" class="summary-thumbnail-image" data-image="https://static1.squarespace.com/static/50c9c50fe4b0a97682fac903/51dc6f4ae4b0a512f81e72c3/5992cd31be42d61afe0f249a/1514702909113/Depositphotos_73335585_m-2015.jpg" data-image-dimensions="1000x883" data-image-focal-point="0.5,0.5" data-load="false" data-src="https://static1.squarespace.com/static/50c9c50fe4b0a97682fac903/51dc6f4ae4b0a512f81e72c3/5992cd31be42d61afe0f249a/1514702909113/Depositphotos_73335585_m-2015.jpg"/>

                    <!-- Title -->
                    <div class="summary-title">
                     <a class="summary-title-link" href="/technology-matters/2017/8/15/so-whats-an-api">
                      So, What's An API?
                     </a>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Metadata (Below Title) -->
                    <div class="summary-metadata-container summary-metadata-container--below-title">
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--primary">
                     </div>
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--secondary">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Excerpt -->
                    <div class="summary-excerpt">
                     <p>
                      In some cases, a software application will need to send data to or receive data from another. How does one achieve this integration between two separate applications built with separate development languages? An application programming interface (API) is a set of routines for achieving this. It specifies how software components should communicate with one another.
                     </p>
                    </div>

                    <div class="summary-excerpt">

                      <img alt="The Difference Between Software Validation and Verification" class="summary-thumbnail-image" data-image="https://static1.squarespace.com/static/50c9c50fe4b0a97682fac903/51dc6f4ae4b0a512f81e72c3/58498c3459cc68cbf7073535/1483691960775/ID-10067389.jpg" data-image-dimensions="400x300" data-image-focal-point="0.5,0.5" data-load="false" data-src="https://static1.squarespace.com/static/50c9c50fe4b0a97682fac903/51dc6f4ae4b0a512f81e72c3/58498c3459cc68cbf7073535/1483691960775/ID-10067389.jpg"/>
                     </div>
                    </a>

                    <div class="summary-metadata-container summary-metadata-container--above-title">

                    <!-- Title -->
                    <div class="summary-title">
                     <a class="summary-title-link" href="/technology-matters/2016/12/8/the-difference-between-software-validation-and-verification">
                      The Difference Between Software Validation and Verification
                     </a>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Metadata (Below Title) -->
                    <div class="summary-metadata-container summary-metadata-container--below-title">
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--primary">
                     </div>
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--secondary">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Excerpt -->
                    <div class="summary-excerpt">
                     <p>
                      Software requirements validation and verification are both complementary processes related to the concepts of quality assurance. Often abbreviated as V&amp;V, the combined process of validation and verification is used in software project management, engineering, and testing to ensure that all specifications are met and the product fulfils its purpose.
                     </p>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Read More Link -->
                    <a class="summary-read-more-link" href="/technology-matters/2016/12/8/the-difference-between-software-validation-and-verification">

                    <!-- Excerpt -->
                    <div class="summary-excerpt">
                     <p>
                      There are different types of software testing approaches, but they all share two common goals: to ensure that the final software meets the requested/agreed upon criteria and is free from bugs, no matter how ideal this may be.                    <!-- Thumbnail -->
                   <div class="summary-thumbnail-outer-container">
                    <a class="summary-thumbnail-container sqs-gallery-image-container" data-description="" data-title="How To Sign Electronic Documents" href="/technology-matters/2015/3/20/how-to-sign-electronic-documents">
                     <div class="summary-thumbnail img-wrapper">
                      <!-- Main Image -->
                      <img alt="How To Sign Electronic Documents" class="summary-thumbnail-image" data-image="https://static1.squarespace.com/static/50c9c50fe4b0a97682fac903/51dc6f4ae4b0a512f81e72c3/550be22ae4b0af84594c1c40/1503207429267/" data-image-dimensions="400x228" data-image-focal-point="0.5,0.5" data-load="false" data-src="https://static1.squarespace.com/static/50c9c50fe4b0a97682fac903/51dc6f4ae4b0a512f81e72c3/550be22ae4b0af84594c1c40/1503207429267/"/>

                    <!-- Title -->
                    <div class="summary-title">
                     <a class="summary-title-link" href="/technology-matters/2015/3/20/how-to-sign-electronic-documents">
                      How To Sign Electronic Documents
                     </a>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Metadata (Below Title) -->
                    <div class="summary-metadata-container summary-metadata-container--below-title">
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--primary">
                     </div>
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--secondary">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Excerpt -->
                    <div class="summary-excerpt">
                     <p style="margin-left:0px; margin-right:0px">
                      <span>
                       Recently, a colleague needed me to append my signature to a document he had emailed to me. It would have been too cumbersome to print out the document, sign it and then scan it back to him so we started looking for options that allowdrawing ones signature, saving it as an image and then inserting it on the electronicdocument.
                      </span>
                      <span>
                       These applications are particularly useful and can be used on projects where stakeholders are geographically dispersed and they need to endorse a document.
                      </span>
                     </p>
                     <p>
                     </p>
                    </div>

                     </a>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Metadata (Below Title) -->

                     <a class="summary-title-link" href="/ba-techniques/2017/9/14/process-performance-metrics">

                     </a>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Metadata (Below Title) -->
                    <div class="summary-metadata-container summary-metadata-container--below-title">

                      Process performance metrics generate accurate data, bringing more efficiency and effectiveness to the decision-making process.                     </div>
                    <!-- Excerpt -->
                    <div class="summary-excerpt">
                     <p>
                      When deciding between different designs, you want to base your decision on rational arguments instead of subjective preferences. One methodology for establishing a procedure to select the best option from multiple available options is Pugh Matrix, also known as the decision matrix.
                     </p>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Read More Link -->
                    <a class="summary-read-more-link" href="/ba-techniques/2017/8/17/introduction-to-pugh-matrix">
                     Read More 
                    </a>

                     </a>

                    <!-- Excerpt -->
                    <div class="summary-excerpt">
                     <p>
                      Consequently, systems developed using the traditional approaches to software development are rigid and difficult to change. Its often necessary to modify a large number of parts of the system just to implement a single, small change. The traditional approaches to software development are effective only in situations where requirements are specific and unlikely to change over time.

                    </div>
                    <!-- Excerpt -->
                    <div class="summary-excerpt">
                     <p>
                      In a perfect world, our plans would always go according to our expectations, and nobody would ever make a wrong decision. Sadly, we dont live in a perfect world, and things dont always go according to plan.                     <!-- Title -->
                    <div class="summary-title">
                     <a class="summary-title-link" href="/ba-techniques/2017/5/20/problemissue-tracking-technique">
                      Problem/Issue Tracking Technique
                     </a>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Metadata (Below Title) -->
                    <div class="summary-metadata-container summary-metadata-container--below-title">
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--primary">
                     </div>
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--secondary">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Excerpt -->
                    <div class="summary-excerpt">
                     <p>
                      This technique is also known as Item tracking or Issue Tracking" and it covers the supervision of defects, assumptions, actions and issues until they are resolved. It provides an opportunity for stakeholders to rank the importance of issues affecting them.
                     </p>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Read More Link -->
                    <a class="summary-read-more-link" href="/ba-techniques/2017/5/20/problemissue-tracking-technique">

                    <!-- Metadata (Below Content) -->

                     </div>
                    </div>
                   </div>
                   <!-- End .summary-content -->
                  </div>
                  <!-- End .summary-item -->
                  <div class=" summary-item summary-item-record-type-text sqs-gallery-design-carousel-slide summary-item-has-thumbnail summary-item-has-excerpt summary-item-has-cats summary-item-has-tags summary-item-has-author summary-item-has-comments-enabled ">
                   <div class="summary-content sqs-gallery-meta-container">
                    <!-- Metadata (Above Title) -->
                    <div class="summary-metadata-container summary-metadata-container--above-title">
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--primary">
                     </div>
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--secondary">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Title -->
                    <div class="summary-title">
                     <a class="summary-title-link" href="/ba-techniques/2017/5/3/project-estimation-techniques-business-analysts-should-know-about-">
                      Project Estimation Techniques Business Analysts Should Know About
                     </a>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Metadata (Below Title) -->
                    <div class="summary-metadata-container summary-metadata-container--below-title">
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--primary">
                     </div>
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--secondary">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Excerpt -->
                    <div class="summary-excerpt">
                     <p>
                      In developing a business case or a feasibility study, many activities are associated with inherent uncertainties and therefore, estimating the resources required to complete such project activities can be a challenging task for the business analyst.
                     </p>
                     <p>
                      Great project estimation commonly involves applying one or more techniques in arriving at time and cost estimations, some of which are discussed in this article.
                     </p>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Read More Link -->
                    <a class="summary-read-more-link" href="/ba-techniques/2017/5/3/project-estimation-techniques-business-analysts-should-know-about-">
                     Read More 
                    </a>
                    <!-- Metadata (Below Content) -->
                    <div class="summary-metadata-container summary-metadata-container--below-content">
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--primary">
                     </div>
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--secondary">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                   </div>
                   <!-- End .summary-content -->
                  </div>
                  <!-- End .summary-item -->
                  <div class=" summary-item summary-item-record-type-text sqs-gallery-design-carousel-slide summary-item-has-thumbnail summary-item-has-excerpt summary-item-has-cats summary-item-has-tags summary-item-has-author summary-item-has-comments-enabled ">
                   <div class="summary-content sqs-gallery-meta-container">
                    <!-- Metadata (Above Title) -->
                    <div class="summary-metadata-container summary-metadata-container--above-title">
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--primary">
                     </div>
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--secondary">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Title -->
                    <div class="summary-title">
                     <a class="summary-title-link" href="/ba-techniques/2017/5/1/vrin-frameworkvrio-analysis">
                      VRIN Framework/VRIO Analysis
                     </a>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Metadata (Below Title) -->
                    <div class="summary-metadata-container summary-metadata-container--below-title">
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--primary">
                     </div>
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--secondary">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Excerpt -->
                    <div class="summary-excerpt">
                     <p>
                      Business analysts can use VRIO to accurately assess the internal resources of a business, its competitive advantage potential, and the possibilities of improvement of relevant resources within key business areas.
                     </p>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Read More Link -->
                    <a class="summary-read-more-link" href="/ba-techniques/2017/5/1/vrin-frameworkvrio-analysis">
                     Read More 
                    </a>

                   <div class="summary-content sqs-gallery-meta-container">

                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--primary">

                    <!-- Title -->
                    <div class="summary-title">
                     <a class="summary-title-link" href="/ba-techniques/2017/4/12/what-bas-can-learn-from-using-personas-in-product-design">
                      What BAs Can Learn from Using Personas in Product Design
                     </a>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Metadata (Below Title) -->
                    <div class="summary-metadata-container summary-metadata-container--below-title">
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--primary">
                     </div>
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--secondary">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Excerpt -->
                    <div class="summary-excerpt">
                     <p>
                      Personas are particularly useful because they serve the purpose of constantly reminding the design team whom they are building the solution for, plus they are easier to remember since theres a story behind each persona.
                     </p>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Read More Link -->
                    <a class="summary-read-more-link" href="/ba-techniques/2017/4/12/what-bas-can-learn-from-using-personas-in-product-design">

                    <!-- Title -->
                    <div class="summary-title">
                     <a class="summary-title-link" href="/ba-techniques/2017/3/26/use-of-personas-in-software-development">
                      Use Of Personas In Software Development
                     </a>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Metadata (Below Title) -->
                    <div class="summary-metadata-container summary-metadata-container--below-title">
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--primary">
                     </div>
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--secondary">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Excerpt -->
                    <div class="summary-excerpt">
                     <p>
                      Initially
                      <a href="http://dev.cooper.com/journal/2016/10/the_origin_of_personas">
                       introduced by Alan Cooper
                      </a>
                      , an American software designer and programmer who is widely known as the Father of Visual Basic, personas are examples of fictitious users who represent a subset of users.
                     </p>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Read More Link -->
                    <a class="summary-read-more-link" href="/ba-techniques/2017/3/26/use-of-personas-in-software-development">
                     Read More

                   <div class="summary-content sqs-gallery-meta-container">

                    <!-- Title -->
                    <div class="summary-title">
                     <a class="summary-title-link" href="/ba-techniques/2017/2/26/relevance-of-the-pdca-plan-do-check-act-methodology-to-software-process-improvement-projects">
                      Relevance Of The PDCA (Plan -Do -Check -Act) Methodology To Software &amp; Process Improvement Projects
                     </a>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Metadata (Below Title) -->
                    <div class="summary-metadata-container summary-metadata-container--below-title">
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--primary">
                     </div>
                     <div class="summary-metadata summary-metadata--secondary">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Excerpt -->
                    <div class="summary-excerpt">
                     <p>
                      The PDCA methodology is an iterative management methodology that is deceptively simple to implement yet frequently overlooked.
                     </p>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Read More Link -->
                    <a class="summary-read-more-link" href="/ba-techniques/2017/2/26/relevance-of-the-pdca-plan-do-check-act-methodology-to-software-process-improvement-projects">

                    <div class="summary-title">

                      Kotter's 8-Step Change Model
                     </a>
                    </div>
                    <!-- Metadata (Below Title) -->
                    <div class="summary-metadata-container summary-metadata-container--below-title">

                    <div class="summary-excerpt">
                     <p>
                      Commonly referred to as Kotter's 8-Step Change Model, this change management strategy describes eight steps organizations must take to enhance their ability to implement change initiatives successfully.
